First appears very much like a CASJ - strongly blue and good necklace and curved culmen/big bill. Specifically, the underparts and undertail coverts appear more whitish-gray than the duskier gray I would expect in a pure Woodhouses, and the back looks much more brown than gray to me. Other features like bill size and shape, extent of supercilium and breastband seem to be in the intermediate range. This is, I believe, within the intergrade zone for these two species where neither seems to be terribly likely or common (or the area just doesnt have that much birder coverage). This particular individual was foraging alone in a relatively small mountain mahogany stand, only vocalized once and was fairly unperturbed by my presence (this could be considered evidence in favor of California, I suppose). Not really any PJ anywhere close but a fair bit of mountain mahogany in the general area.
